  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_942b2370-de2e-41f8-897c-c660a4555bf6'

<span id="freeTextContainer6153406756230618014"><b>Six months in the life of the world's most dangerous teenager.</b><br/><br/><i>Youth in Revolt</i> is the journals of Nick Twisp, California's most precocious diarist, whose ongoing struggles to make sense out of high school, deal with his divorced parents, and lose his virginity result in his transformation from an unassuming fourteen-year-old to a modern youth in open revolt. <br/><br/>As his family s</span>
  <span id="freeText6153406756230618014" style="display:none"><b>Six months in the life of the world's most dangerous teenager.</b><br /><br /><i>Youth in Revolt</i> is the journals of Nick Twisp, California's most precocious diarist, whose ongoing struggles to make sense out of high school, deal with his divorced parents, and lose his virginity result in his transformation from an unassuming fourteen-year-old to a modern youth in open revolt. <br /><br />As his family splinters, worlds collide, and the police block all routes out of town, Nick must cope with economic deprivation, homelessness, the gulag of the public schools, a competitive Type-A father, murderous canines (in triplicate), and an inconvenient hair trigger on his erectile response—all while vying ardently for the affections of the beauteous Sheeni Saunders, teenage goddess and ultimate intellectual goad.</span>

<div id="review_2261410562" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2261410562" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2261410562?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=humorous-fiction">humorous-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=characters-i-want-to-slap">characters-i-want-to-slap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2261410562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12851658659871429271"><b>"Nick," she said, when I had finished, "six months ago you were just another brownnosing honor student. What happened?"</b><br/><br/>What happened was Nick fell in <s>love</s> lust with Sheeni, and would do anything, ANYTHING to <s>be by her side</s> get into her pants. Anything may or may not include lying, cheating, screwing over his friends, trickery, forgery, transvestism, doping another's drinks, grand theft auto, vandalism, becoming a fugitive from justice, and so many more offenses it would take nearly 500 pages to </span>
  <span id="freeText12851658659871429271" style="display:none"><b>"Nick," she said, when I had finished, "six months ago you were just another brownnosing honor student. What happened?"</b><br /><br />What happened was Nick fell in <s>love</s> lust with Sheeni, and would do anything, ANYTHING to <s>be by her side</s> get into her pants. Anything may or may not include lying, cheating, screwing over his friends, trickery, forgery, transvestism, doping another's drinks, grand theft auto, vandalism, becoming a fugitive from justice, and so many more offenses it would take nearly 500 pages to tell you about them. You probably gathered that Nick is a horrible person who, if the feds don't get him first, will eventually end up in the White House. <br /><br />And, yet . . . I laughed my head off at his antics. It helps that nearly everyone else in Nick's life is equally awful. His divorced parents are the pits - self-involved and negligent, and the unattainable goddess Sheeni keeps Nick at arms length, saving him as a sort of back-up plan if she can't get the man she really wants. <br /><br />Why, it's enough to make a guy want to commit a felony or two (or five.)<br /><br />As I've mentioned many times, I am easily amused. <i>You</i> may not find this book quite as funny as I did, particularly if you're fond of likable characters. <i>You</i> may also be horrified by so many sexually active 14-year-olds. (I wasn't doing this shit when I was 14. Maybe that's why I was just a brownnosing <i>average</i> student.) <i>You</i> may not like this novel, but for me, it was the right book at the right time.<br /><br />Nick's hijinks continue in two more books, but after 500 pages, even I've had enough of him for now.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3199798972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3199798972" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3199798972?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=california">california</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3199798972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7070551799800257440"><i>Youth in Revolt</i> had some funny moments here and there, but mostly it was just painfully crude, pretentious and annoying. I come across "comedy" YA novels like this from time to time, and they're sort of a hit or miss when it comes to how actually witty and creative they happen to be. More often than not, they're just vulgar and bizarre. A pseudo-intellectual fourteen-year-old boy trying to impress a girl who's out of his league for I'm sure you can guess what reason, well, it really isn't the ty</span>
  <span id="freeText7070551799800257440" style="display:none"><i>Youth in Revolt</i> had some funny moments here and there, but mostly it was just painfully crude, pretentious and annoying. I come across "comedy" YA novels like this from time to time, and they're sort of a hit or miss when it comes to how actually witty and creative they happen to be. More often than not, they're just vulgar and bizarre. A pseudo-intellectual fourteen-year-old boy trying to impress a girl who's out of his league for I'm sure you can guess what reason, well, it really isn't the type of thing that I find amusing. I'm not a prude, but seriously?<br /><br />I saw the film adaptation a number of years ago at some birthday party I went to. What's intended to be comedic in either version of the story usually just comes off as awkward, gross and strange. <i>Youth in Revolt</i> is like a Wes Anderson film mangled with an issue of Playboy Magazine, all rolled up into a novel. It follows the life of Nick Twisp and his misadventures with school, his dysfunctional family and his attempts to lose his virginity to Sheeni Saunders, a girl whose intellect surpasses his own. The book version differs quite a bit in events and scenery, and the book also heaps on the pretentiousness much more than the film does. While this is intended to be funny, it's really just obnoxious, unrealistic and boring.<br /><br />I think what makes this book work for many readers is its shock value and target audience. A raunchy story of sex and dysfunction where the kids are smarter than the adults will offend parents and draw in teen readers. It's everything that parents and school districts <i>wouldn't</i> want kids to be reading. When I was growing up, there was Stephen King's <i>It</i> with the infamous teenage sewer orgy scene, which no parent ever let their kids in town borrow from the library. As a story, its "humour" only works insofar as the reader can tolerate some boy's musings on his own crotch, and numerous references to university-grade phrases and ramblings that no kid that age would know anything about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7070551799800257440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3199798972">

  <span id="freeText11188672990916035519" style="display:none">Oh, no. No. Absolutely not, this book is not for me and I refuse to read 400 more pages of this crap (especially not when reviews allude to it being 400 more pages of the same sort of thing). Constant boners and mocking your middle-aged mother's appearance are not funny. <br /><br /><i>But Rachel! Didn't you like Portnoy's Complaint?</i><br /><br />Yeah. But Alexander Portnoy wasn't like "lol, my mother has blue veins!" He was like "lol, my girlfriend is ignorant and can't spell." Both mocks are mean-spirited, but at least one of them is mocking a quality that is changeable, thus coming off a little less than ragingly chauvinistic.<br /><br /><i>But Rachel! Isn't Nick Twisp just a 14 year old boy? Isn't sexism par for the course? </i><br /><br />Is a 14 year old boy who can correctly use the words "suzerainty" and "inviolate" par for the course as well, then? Didn't think so.<br /><br />I know it's supposed to be absurd, but I still don't think it's funny. If 500 pages is a slog for people who actually enjoy this book, then I am, as Amy would say, getting the boop out now.</span>

<div id="review_466733170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466733170" />
    <a title="Alex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10095190-alex"><img alt="Alex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339222813p2/10095190.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466733170?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/10095190-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10095190-alex?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466733170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3851452804695326095">Fate. This book and I were destined to be together.<br/><br/>We were first brought together when I was just 13 years old, rummaging through the discount shelves at Barnes and Noble in Indianapolis. The cover drew me in, and I sat my tween butt down on the floor and started reading. I made it about twenty or so pages in, feeling my face flush at reading about S-E-X in a public place, and likely matching the color of the lower half of the title letters when my mom found me hidden in the aisle. She asked if </span>
  <span id="freeText3851452804695326095" style="display:none">Fate. This book and I were destined to be together.<br /><br />We were first brought together when I was just 13 years old, rummaging through the discount shelves at Barnes and Noble in Indianapolis. The cover drew me in, and I sat my tween butt down on the floor and started reading. I made it about twenty or so pages in, feeling my face flush at reading about S-E-X in a public place, and likely matching the color of the lower half of the title letters when my mom found me hidden in the aisle. She asked if I was okay, and why was I acting so weird, and I don't remember how I responded. We left for home, and shortly thereafter, moved across the country, the book gone but not forgotten.<br /><br />Three years later, I stumbled across it on yet another sale shelf, this time at the famed Powell's City of Books in my new hometown of Portland, OR. Upon spotting that unforgettable cover, I knew I couldn't let the book slip out of my life another time and bought it immediately.<br /><br />I often talk about how I can't put books down, and I tend to rate a lot of books highly, but I am now 30 years old and still consider this to be my favorite book of all time, for ever and ever and all of eternity, with sprinkles and a cherry on top. Not only could I not put this down, I immediately re-read it after the first read, and have read it again and again, nearly every year since.<br /><br />It's not that anything in the book is particularly <i>realistic</i>, but that's really why it's so captivating. It's completely ridiculous and off the wall, and nothing in the book would ever actually happen. There is nobody in the world who actually acts like Nick Twisp, but he's so damned entertaining to read about, I don't care. He's hilarious, he's intelligent yet completely stupid all at the same time, and his misadventures are perfect. The entire cast of characters (caricatures, really) in this book are perfect, each and every one.<br /><br />Honestly, I am hard-pressed to come up with one bad thing to say about this book. If I could marry a book, I would marry Youth in Revolt, and live happily ever after.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3851452804695326095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16806386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16806386" />
    <a title="Erica Satifka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120870-erica-satifka"><img alt="Erica Satifka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470988304p2/120870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16806386?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica Satifka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica Satifka" href="/user/show/120870-erica-satifka">Erica Satifka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA fans, humor fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16806386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3016190956691351805">Not your average coming of age novel, C.D. Payne's trilogy of short novels about the travails of young journaler Nick Twisp has a comic wit and intricate plot twists that can be enjoyed by people of all ages.<br/><br/>This boy meets girl plot centers on Nick, a bookish, sex-crazed 14-year-old, and Sheeni Saunders, a Francophile sociopath who juggles men and has a taste for expensive clothing and jewelry. Keeping them apart are Sheeni's ultra-religious parents and four hundred miles of California coast lin</span>
  <span id="freeText3016190956691351805" style="display:none">Not your average coming of age novel, C.D. Payne's trilogy of short novels about the travails of young journaler Nick Twisp has a comic wit and intricate plot twists that can be enjoyed by people of all ages.<br /><br />This boy meets girl plot centers on Nick, a bookish, sex-crazed 14-year-old, and Sheeni Saunders, a Francophile sociopath who juggles men and has a taste for expensive clothing and jewelry. Keeping them apart are Sheeni's ultra-religious parents and four hundred miles of California coast line, both of which Nick is desperate to trump by any means necessary. Though it is true that Nick and his "One and Only Love" Sheeni are both fairly unsympathetic characters, you'll still find yourself caught up in their love affair, which Nick keeps aflame by the careful use of several split personalities and multiple criminal actions.<br /><br />The real gem of these books, however, are the minor characters: Sheeni's semiomniscient brother Paul, always two steps ahead of Nick's schemes; Nick's revolting (yet strangely sweet) roommate Dwayne; the painfully shy trucker Wally Rumpkin, who possesses an eidetic memory; and a trio of identical dogs named after existentialist French writers. Even more than Plot A, these little touches around the sides are what makes this novel charming and a cut above average YA fiction. There have been several sequels and I'm definitely putting them on my to-read list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3016190956691351805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101452425" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101452425" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2615088-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101452425?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/2615088-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101452425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16160093393861506770"><br/>If there is one thing--ONE THING--that you can take away from this book, it is this:<br/><br/>BOYS WILL LITERALLY GO TO ANY LENGTHS TO GET IN YOUR PANTS.<br/><br/>We are talking federal laws here, people.<br/><br/>And I loved every second of it.<br/><br/>We first get a glimpse of Nick's dry, at times wicked humor, from the opening sentence:<br/><br/><br/>WEDNESDAY, July 18--My name is Nick. Someday, if I grow up to be a gangster, perhaps I will be known as Nick the Prick. This may cause some embarrassment to my family, but when your don gives you yo</span>
  <span id="freeText16160093393861506770" style="display:none"><br />If there is one thing--ONE THING--that you can take away from this book, it is this:<br /><br />BOYS WILL LITERALLY GO TO ANY LENGTHS TO GET IN YOUR PANTS.<br /><br />We are talking federal laws here, people.<br /><br />And I loved every second of it.<br /><br />We first get a glimpse of Nick's dry, at times wicked humor, from the opening sentence:<br /><br /><br />WEDNESDAY, July 18--My name is Nick. Someday, if I grow up to be a gangster, perhaps I will be known as Nick the Prick. This may cause some embarrassment to my family, but when your don gives you your mafia sobriquet you don't ask questions.<br /><br /><br />Assuming that that paragraph alone did not convince you to go out and purchase Youth in Revolt, I shall continue.<br /><br />Nick introduces himself quiet plainly, leaving nothing sacred, unabashedly saying what every other boy in the world is thinking--he hates his name, he hates his family, and he is obsessed with sex.<br /><br />Now, I'm going to get it out there right now. Youth in Revolt is not for everyone--in fact, most people will find it a revolting (excuse the pun), raunchy, Judd Apatow-movie gone awry collection of paper and words that doesn't deserve the title of 'book'. Most people will grimace and toss it into the fireplace and try to erase it from their virgin minds. Some. Not all. <br /><br />So, if you have no been frightened off, let's continue.<br /><br />This begins with typical teen ranting--it is a diary, after all--with Nick generally introducing himself, his family, and his interests. It's hilarious right from the starts, from Nick coming home from his father's house to find his mother has painted his bedroom pink to help "calm" him--"she said she had read this color was widely used in hospitals to help calm mental patients. I told her I wasn't mentally ill, I was just a teenager"--to his vocal disdain for Jerry, his obese step father. Youth in Revolt is basically the extreme side of white trash, told through the eyes of a kid destined for greater things.<br /><br />Nick is positive that he will remain a virgin forever, until an unexpected trip to a trailer park up in Lakeport sends him head-first into the Greater Then Thou Sheeni Saunders. Beautiful, intellegent and a tad mamnipulative, she takes Nick's heart in a deadly chokehold and refuses to let go. While it's hard to imagine as you get deeper into the novel, she really is the reason Nick does anything. He has literally broken near every law in the country beside first degree murder (notice I don't say murder--I say first degree murder) just to get some. While some would argue that this cannot suffice as a plot, it most certainly can. And it does. <br /><br />So, as Nick leaves with Sheeni's promise of you-know-what still fresh in his mind, he resolves to bring her to him and lose his ever-loving virginity before his freshman year is up. <br /><br />So, without giving anything away, I will just declare my undivided love of YOUTH IN REVOLT and how GODDAMN HILARIOUS IT IS.<br /><br />The writing, as I can describe it, is the way I'd imagine a hyper-intellegent, hyper-sexual, and hyper-neurotic teenager would write. Big words rule the day in this satirical look on modern youth as Nick attempts to understand why the fuck everyone is SO DAMN CRAZY and how he managed to be counted among them.<br /><br />In a period of six months, Nick goes from a meak, bookish virgin to a crossdressing stud with a bit of a complex. Hell yes.<br /><br /><br /><br />Nick is not a hero--he's an anti-hero. He's a bit of a jerk, crude, just plain nasty at times, but you there's a feeling of devotion to him that few authors could pull off--you HAVE to cheer for him, you HAVE to sympathize with him, you HAVE to wish him well, because there is simply no one else to root for. He is literally the only boat of sanity in a crazy, mixed up world and, no matter how he reacts to the world around him, he is simply the only one we, the reader, can root for because he's the one telling the story. <br /><br />As for the other characters, they're all described basically as morons--except for Sheeni--and this may be a sign of an unreliable narrator. That's another thing--we don't know if this is true, we don't know if Nick's telling the truth about anything, or just lying to convince himself there's a legit reason he ends up where he is. We just have to trust him.<br /><br />Mr. Payne does a perfect job in dramatizing modern youth and making fun of the lengths some boys will go too to get what they want. He lightens up what could be a heavy situation, pokes fun very discreetly at modern youth and sex, and just flat-out rocks my world. A must-read for anyone with a sense of humor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16160093393861506770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_101688509" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101688509" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2324650-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254535447p2/2324650.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101688509?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/2324650-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101688509" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4322906004168705199">Wow, this book is amazing. It's definitely different and it is so great. I loved mostly every minute of Youth In Revolt. You will laugh, you will cry, there will be lots of moments where you will cringe, others you will cry out in surprise. Youth in Revolt is definitely not a book for the faint-hearted. But in saying that it truly is worth a read.<br/><br/>Just a quick warning that I would say this book should be read by 16 year olds and over. There are several scenes that aren't entirely appropriate. I m</span>
  <span id="freeText4322906004168705199" style="display:none">Wow, this book is amazing. It's definitely different and it is so great. I loved mostly every minute of Youth In Revolt. You will laugh, you will cry, there will be lots of moments where you will cringe, others you will cry out in surprise. Youth in Revolt is definitely not a book for the faint-hearted. But in saying that it truly is worth a read.<br /><br />Just a quick warning that I would say this book should be read by 16 year olds and over. There are several scenes that aren't entirely appropriate. I managed to overlook those scenes because the rest of the story is brilliant.<br /><br />Nick is such a refreshing character. I don't usually compare books to other books but if I had to describe Nick and his diary I would say it's like an American version of Adrian Mole with a lot more antics and 'typical adolescent behaviour'. But in saying that, I do believe I got a lot more laughs from Nick.<br /><br />While the book is 499 pages, don't let that deter you, it's split into three books. Each book deals with a different persona so to speak. I have to say that it did start off a little slow but once it got into the story it kind of turned into a snowball effect where the events kept growing and growing and spiralling out of control.<br /><br />So many of the characters in this book are unusual and extremely interesting characters. There are too many to name, you basically have to read this book. It is one of the best books I've read all year.<br /><br />One thing I must add about this book is that it is extremely dated, but that just kind of sets the scene a bit more and I thought it added to the comedy of the book.<br /><br />I liked the ending of Youth In Revolt, it didn't leave a wide open ending and it didn't close it completely either. I know that there is indeed a sequel and I'm thinking that I'll definitely pick it up one day. There's also a movie based on Youth In Revolt and it's called Youth In Revolt so I'd be really interested in seeing that.<br /><br />Overall, Youth In Revolt is one book that is worth the read at least once in everyone lives.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4322906004168705199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_368991405" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/368991405" />
    <a title="René" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2304631-ren"><img alt="René" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605885915p2/2304631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/368991405?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="René" class="user" itemprop="url" name="René" href="/user/show/2304631-ren">René</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer368991405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11123565538478120866">This is really a peculiar read.<br/><br/>It's the journal of Nick Twisp, a manipulative, cynical, sex-obsessed youth whose erstwhile (I'm using that word because the author likes it so much) good behavior is succombing to the adolescent prime imperative of losing one's virginity. He hones in on his new amour Shinee, who is willing, experienced and cooperative, though enigmatically distant and drifting. Things get in the way, obstacles made of arbitrary parental actions and decisions, space, timing, his co</span>
  <span id="freeText11123565538478120866" style="display:none">This is really a peculiar read.<br /><br />It's the journal of Nick Twisp, a manipulative, cynical, sex-obsessed youth whose erstwhile (I'm using that word because the author likes it so much) good behavior is succombing to the adolescent prime imperative of losing one's virginity. He hones in on his new amour Shinee, who is willing, experienced and cooperative, though enigmatically distant and drifting. Things get in the way, obstacles made of arbitrary parental actions and decisions, space, timing, his constrictive teen existence, his lack of economic freedom.<br /><br />I found this book very funny. Nick's über-logical approach to things make him undertake courses of action that made me cringe and squirm and giggle (think fellatio with his best male friend), and it occurred to me that, had I read this book as an actual teen I would have been rather shocked. I myself was as rational a teen as Nick is, but I wasn't one to brave borders and stand up to adults. Much. Well, maybe a little, but not in any way as much as Nick. But Nick has no real respect for adults, he's an adult trapped in an adolescent body and in an adolescent's life. As such, being a virgin at his ripe old age of 14 seems to him egregious, and the end will justify all means at his disposal (and then some).<br /><br />It seems that this is less a believable account of a 14-year-old than the attempt of the same character at 40 to rewrite his past. That would illuminate the latent understanding of adult intentions and levers, the self-deprecating humor, and the candid avowal of the utter simplicity of what he wants: sexual congress, as soon as possible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11123565538478120866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=humor-comedy">humor-comedy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=young-adult-genre">young-adult-genre</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993251855" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13921853532819014510">I knew that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10050.Youth_in_Revolt_The_Journals_of_Nick_Twisp' title='Youth in Revolt The Journals of Nick Twisp by C.D. Payne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Youth in Revolt</a> is a movie but I didn't realize it was based on a book until I saw the audiobook available at my library. I have never watched the movie but was excited to try a slightly different book than I'm used to. I have to say I really enjoyed it! The book is a collection of journal entries written by the lead character Nick Twisp. I thought this book was pretty hilarious even though the entries written by a hormone-crazed, fourteen-year-old boy were a little over the top. But</span>
  <span id="freeText13921853532819014510" style="display:none">I knew that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10050.Youth_in_Revolt_The_Journals_of_Nick_Twisp" title="Youth in Revolt The Journals of Nick Twisp by C.D. Payne" rel="nofollow noopener">Youth in Revolt</a> is a movie but I didn't realize it was based on a book until I saw the audiobook available at my library. I have never watched the movie but was excited to try a slightly different book than I'm used to. I have to say I really enjoyed it! The book is a collection of journal entries written by the lead character Nick Twisp. I thought this book was pretty hilarious even though the entries written by a hormone-crazed, fourteen-year-old boy were a little over the top. But who knows, maybe this is really how some teenage boys think! Regardless, that aspect added to the hilarity, as crude as it was at times. Nick, who was once a confused and innocent young teen ends the story as a rebellious young man on a mission. He is in "open revolt" as referenced in the title. Family, high school, and virginity issues can apparently have that effect...go figure.<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>“Consider, if you will, the morning boner. What a metaphor of hope and renewal! How can anyone give way to despair when one’s groin greets each day with such a gala spectacle of physical optimism?”</i></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/150648-tiffany?shelf=nancysruleof50">nancysruleof50</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4353068" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15056682988213730958">The friend who recommended this to me is a guy. He likes coming-of-age-guy stuff (mainly movies and books). He LOVED the movie <i>Rushmore</i>, and when I said I'd seen it but didn't like it, his answer was something to the effect of "Maybe you had to be a teenage boy to appreciate it." When he recommended this book and told me how much he loved it, he added "You might have needed to have been a teenaged male to appreciate this book."<br/><br/>Twenty or so pages in, and I can see why you'd probably need to be a </span>
  <span id="freeText15056682988213730958" style="display:none">The friend who recommended this to me is a guy. He likes coming-of-age-guy stuff (mainly movies and books). He LOVED the movie <i>Rushmore</i>, and when I said I'd seen it but didn't like it, his answer was something to the effect of "Maybe you had to be a teenage boy to appreciate it." When he recommended this book and told me how much he loved it, he added "You might have needed to have been a teenaged male to appreciate this book."<br /><br />Twenty or so pages in, and I can see why you'd probably need to be a teenage boy to like this book: bragging about/hoping for male anatomy, fantasizing about female anatomy, talking about his zits, calling his mom stupid. I can see a few good moments to it, but overall, I think maybe you have to have been a teenage boy to like this. But in past tense (like, I'm not sure a teenage boy should read it), after you've outgrown all that stuff and can see in hindsight that the way he talks is utterly stupid and disrespectful. Maybe? We'll see how it goes.<br /><br />... Strangely, though, it's not a *terrible* book, especially if you skip over or try not to think too much about the horny, know-it-all, hates-fat-girls teenage boy parts of the story. The rest is a series of comic flubs in life.<br /><br />.... And yet, I've decided to stop reading. At one point, I decided I was curious whether Nick ever got together with his dream girl (or any other girl; perhaps a new dream girl), but then I realized I didn't actually *care*. Curious, yes; care, no. So I stopped reading it. Halfway through the book, I stopped. There are too many other books out there to spend my time reading a book I'm only mildly curious about.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5483363262458014559">It didn't work for me. While I understand that teenage boys think about sex every minute of every day... the main character of Nick is a grating personality that takes the fun out of sex. If his plotting only backfired on himself, I might have enjoyed it more; but the weasel victimizes his friends, his annoying parents, and completely innocent people. While I laugh and love annoying jerkish characters in many Adult Swim offerings (see: Aqua Teen Hunger Force & Frisky Dingo), those shows are so o</span>
  <span id="freeText5483363262458014559" style="display:none">It didn't work for me. While I understand that teenage boys think about sex every minute of every day... the main character of Nick is a grating personality that takes the fun out of sex. If his plotting only backfired on himself, I might have enjoyed it more; but the weasel victimizes his friends, his annoying parents, and completely innocent people. While I laugh and love annoying jerkish characters in many Adult Swim offerings (see: Aqua Teen Hunger Force &amp; Frisky Dingo), those shows are so outlandish that the joke is how OPPOSITE of true behaviour the characters employ. But in this novel, Payne tries to combine the very real emotions of youth AND a very unreal plot. So I couldn't laugh. <br /><br />And there isn't a true driving plot, rather a series of vignettes each more improbable than the next. So the story doesn't build momentum.<br /><br />One final note: The film version of this book just came out with Michael Cera as the lead. While I haven't seen the movie, the casting feels wrong. Cera was so hilarious in Arrested Development &amp; Superbad at playing a smart yet naive,timid teenagers (with the character's intelligence creating the timid nature -- I can't do this because of the trouble I'd be in if I get caught). But the lead character Nick Twisp in this novel is a smart yet naive, reckless teenager (with the character's intelligence causing the reckless nature -- I have to do this, because I'll never get caught... and another scheme to cover the original scheme will work even better) I don't see how timid Michael Cera can play Max Fischer from Rushmore. <br /><br />Grade: C<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_132653139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132653139" />
    <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews"><img alt="YA Reads Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285429046p2/1764232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132653139?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YA Reads Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YA Reads Book Reviews" href="/user/show/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews">YA Reads Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1764232-ya-reads-book-reviews?shelf=kiona">kiona</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132653139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14497791576354296813">Youth in Revolt is unlike any other YA novel. It’s crude, honest, and hysterical. Payne has painted a wonderful picture of a young boy coming to terms with himself. What sets Youth in Revolt apart from other novels in the genre – beside its frank descriptions of an adolescent boy’s mind – is an element of absurdity. Payne weaves a playfulness into his characters and their actions that makes for a story so interesting you can’t help but read to the end.<br/><br/>Though the novel deals with boys around the </span>
  <span id="freeText14497791576354296813" style="display:none">Youth in Revolt is unlike any other YA novel. It’s crude, honest, and hysterical. Payne has painted a wonderful picture of a young boy coming to terms with himself. What sets Youth in Revolt apart from other novels in the genre – beside its frank descriptions of an adolescent boy’s mind – is an element of absurdity. Payne weaves a playfulness into his characters and their actions that makes for a story so interesting you can’t help but read to the end.<br /><br />Though the novel deals with boys around the age of fourteen, it is intended for an older audience. Payne does not shy away from topics such as sex, drugs, and alcohol. In fact, he goes into detail about these subjects, creating a realistic portrayal of a young boy’s mind. This immediately grabbed my interest, as there are so few male narrators left to the YA genre and, of those narrators, so few provide honest depictions of the male psyche.<br /><br />The story is given to us in the format of Nick Twisp’s journal. We learn that, though Nick is only fourteen years old, he is highly intelligent. His vocabulary rivals that of a college student and his wit resonates with older readers. Younger readers will be entertained by his displays of immaturity and fool-hardy pranks that land him in trouble so unrealistic that you want to believe it just so you can laugh. But if you don’t laugh at Nick’s pranks, you’ll have to laugh at his mother’s behavior and her numerous crazy boyfriends.<br /><br />The delight of Youth in Revolt lies not only in Nick’s unique voice, but in the extravagant journey he takes. This is not your typical boy-meets-girl story. It’s more of a boy-will-travel-to-the-ends-of-the-earth-for-girl story. Nick journeys from state to state pursuing the girl he believes to be his soul mate. Throughout his journey to reunite with Sheeni, Nick meets quite a few characters – some friends, many enemies, and some he can’t even identify. One of his most memorable enemies is Trent, Sheeni’s ex-boyfriend. Trent is still very much in love with Sheeni and determined to win her back. Nick knows he is no match for Trent’s intelligence, wealth, and good looks so he concocts plan after plan to keep Sheeni and Trent apart. His plans often backfire and have the reverse affect of bringing the two together. Nick’s quest for Sheeni’s affection is the underlying main plot. After reading about the lengths Nick will go to for Sheeni, you’ll be rooting for him by the end.<br /><br />Perhaps the most unique twist to the story is Nick’s creation of an alter-ego, Francois Dillinger. Francois is an evil master-mind, a part of Nick willing to push boundaries and even break the law. Nick lets Francois take the reigns whenever he feels he can’t handle a situation because Francois isn’t afraid to tell people off or run away from home. This book is already on a level all its own and the addition of Francois bumps it up one more level. If you’re looking for a mature, laugh-out-loud YA novel, you’ve found it in Youth in Revolt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14497791576354296813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Wcpalmergmail.com" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2989010-wcpalmergmail-com"><img alt="Wcpalmergmail.com" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79241916?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wcpalmergmail.com" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wcpalmergmail.com" href="/user/show/2989010-wcpalmergmail-com">Wcpalmergmail.com</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79241916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2038851396882675147">A modern day Confederacy of Dunces, and equally worthy of praise. Nick Twisp is a younger, leaner, sex-addicted Ignatius J. Reilly. The book is composed of Twisp's highly-literate (especially for a 14 year-old) journal entries, only Twisp uses all of his cunning linguistics (pun intended) to espouse on masturbation and the pursuit of intercourse - and what a pursuit it is. Considering the quest to conquer virginity pretty much sums up the subject matter, you would think that Youth in Revolt migh</span>
  <span id="freeText2038851396882675147" style="display:none">A modern day Confederacy of Dunces, and equally worthy of praise. Nick Twisp is a younger, leaner, sex-addicted Ignatius J. Reilly. The book is composed of Twisp's highly-literate (especially for a 14 year-old) journal entries, only Twisp uses all of his cunning linguistics (pun intended) to espouse on masturbation and the pursuit of intercourse - and what a pursuit it is. Considering the quest to conquer virginity pretty much sums up the subject matter, you would think that Youth in Revolt might be a tad self-indulgent at 500 pages. You would be correct. However, it's fitting, as "Self-Indulgent" might as well be our protagonist's middle name. Not to mention that the book is laugh-out-loud hilarious on every page, as Twisp's adventures become increasingly outlandish with each journal entry. Loved it.<br />P.S. There's a movie adaptation due out soon, starring Hollywood's "IT BOY 2007-?" Michael Cera. Apparently studio execs decided that every character from age 16-25 must be incredibly introverted and awkward at all times, or a sparkling androgynous vampire. I hate to say it, but it kind of makes me miss Corey Feldman.</span>

<div id="review_8927581" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8927581" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/419287-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289534648p2/419287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8927581?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/419287-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">the title says it all</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/419287-jessica?shelf=california-%C3%BCber-alles">california-über-alles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/419287-jessica?shelf=wee-ones-and-bored-teenagers">wee-ones-and-bored-teenagers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/419287-jessica?shelf=leetle-boys">leetle-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8927581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6737283102238387067">This was another book that had its memory kind of ruined for me when I met the author (not the author's fault; unfortunate circumstances). If that hadn't happened, it could well be a five-star.<br/><br/>I know that at the time I read this, I was thoughly convinced it was the most hilarious and entertaining novel I'd ever read in my life (though it is another long one with a somewhat anticlimactic -- hah hah hah -- ending). It's certainly up there with the classics of teenage-angst lit, and Nick Twisp is s</span>
  <span id="freeText6737283102238387067" style="display:none">This was another book that had its memory kind of ruined for me when I met the author (not the author's fault; unfortunate circumstances). If that hadn't happened, it could well be a five-star.<br /><br />I know that at the time I read this, I was thoughly convinced it was the most hilarious and entertaining novel I'd ever read in my life (though it is another long one with a somewhat anticlimactic -- hah hah hah -- ending). It's certainly up there with the classics of teenage-angst lit, and Nick Twisp is so much more than just a horny, enterprising California version of Adrian Mole.... or is he? I don't know really, since I haven't revisited it since the book first came out over a decade ago. However, I'd wholeheartedly recommend this one to anybody between the ages of thirteen and eighteen. Then maybe they can report back, and let me know how it's held up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6737283102238387067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1248075063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1248075063" />
    <a title="Selwa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6874113-selwa"><img alt="Selwa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440130280p2/6874113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248075063?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selwa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selwa" href="/user/show/6874113-selwa">Selwa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6874113-selwa?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6874113-selwa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248075063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12816048498747286324">Please don't pay attention to the time I'm posting this review ... yes, it's nearly 3 am, and yes, I just finished the book 20 minutes ago, but I also had about 4 cups of iced coffee this evening, starting at 8 pm. I'm now convinced sleep is for suckers and anyway tonight was a fine night to finish the book and write the review.<br/><br/>First, some background. This is the story, epistolary style, of a 14-year-old boy by the name of Nick Twisp. His parents are divorced, he doesn't get along with either of</span>
  <span id="freeText12816048498747286324" style="display:none">Please don't pay attention to the time I'm posting this review ... yes, it's nearly 3 am, and yes, I just finished the book 20 minutes ago, but I also had about 4 cups of iced coffee this evening, starting at 8 pm. I'm now convinced sleep is for suckers and anyway tonight was a fine night to finish the book and write the review.<br /><br />First, some background. This is the story, epistolary style, of a 14-year-old boy by the name of Nick Twisp. His parents are divorced, he doesn't get along with either of them anyway, and he's in love with a girl by the name of Sheeni. Hilarity ensues.<br /><br />Now, you may be wondering why a 34-year-old lady would read a book told from the POV of a horny 14 year old. Well, my boyfriend gave me the book, one of his favorites when he himself was a teenager, for my birthday. And I think that right there explains the difference between his 5 stars and my 3. When he read it, he was about 5 years older than the protagonist, and probably related to him in more ways than he'd care to admit now. I'm sure there was a lot of mental high-fiving. I'm 20 years older than Nick (oof, I need to let that sink in), and, in fact, closer in age to his parents. I felt bad for them (for the most part) for having a jerk kid, since at many points I didn't like Nick very much, and felt he brought on his troubles through his own poorly thought out actions (or reactions). Sheeni also came across as bitchy and manipulative somewhat frequently. And most of the adults were moronic.<br /><br />By the end, though, certain characters were redeemed and I'm mostly okay with the ending, though I do find it far-fetched. I'm a little curious about what happens immediately after, but not enough to go pick up the next book in the series (though I might pick it up for the boyfriend ... shhh, don't tell him).<br /><br />Finally, there was one bit that I just could not excuse, and it was a rape scene, complete with a sedative slipped in a drink. I'm not sure why, when a female is raped, it's horrifying, but when a male is raped, it is (occasionally) painted as humorous. I don't like double standards.<br /><br />While I did enjoy the story overall, I'm not sure who I'd recommend it to. I certainly wouldn't hand it over to my 13-year-old nephew. It's quite sexually graphic, and I was caught off guard multiple times, not because I'm squeamish about such things but because I have a hard time imagining a 9th grader thinking these things! But then again I was quite sheltered myself at that age :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12816048498747286324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Someday, if I grow up to be a gangster, Perhaps I will be known as Nick the Prick.This may cause some embarressment for my family, but when your don gives you your mafia sobriquet you dont ask questions.</i><br/><br/>So begins the tale of poor, sex deprived Nick Twisp. From that first line I was hooked completely. Nicks sense of humor and sarcasim are things to be admired. Nick's troubled life and quest to get laid has got to be one of the most entertaining things Ive ever read! <i>Youth In Revo</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9982278187248012997" style="display:none"><i>My name is Nick. Someday, if I grow up to be a gangster, Perhaps I will be known as Nick the Prick.This may cause some embarressment for my family, but when your don gives you your mafia sobriquet you dont ask questions.</i><br /><br />So begins the tale of poor, sex deprived Nick Twisp. From that first line I was hooked completely. Nicks sense of humor and sarcasim are things to be admired. Nick's troubled life and quest to get laid has got to be one of the most entertaining things Ive ever read! <i>Youth In Revolt</i> covers all the teenage hot button topics: sex, drugs, masturbation, pregnancy, dating, arson, suicide, divorce, affairs, the FBI, and split-personalities. One cant help but relate (hehe)!<br /><br />I loved Nick, as previously mentioned, but not so sure about all the different personalities. Francois was marvelous, but Carlotta wasnt the greatest. dont get me wrong, I loved the whole situation there, just not sure if I loved her personally! Sheeni was a great character, but thats all I can say for her. She was a great character, but I couldnt stand her. Though that was more due to the fact that I love poor Nickie and she was definitely using him. Vijay was one of my favorite characters until book 3 (Youth In Exile), when he stabbed Nick in the back. The little slime ball!<br /><br />Anyway, couldnt help but love it! The only problems I encountered were my parents looking at me funny when I randomly laughed or grinned (because really, you cant go 3 lines without cracking up) and the end. I so wished to hear more about Nick!</span>

<div id="review_75116349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75116349" />
    <a title="Blue Milker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1101437-blue-milker"><img alt="Blue Milker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582731286p2/1101437.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75116349?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blue Milker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blue Milker" href="/user/show/1101437-blue-milker">Blue Milker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75116349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14554963491629848515">I'm a bit conflicted about this book.<br/><br/>It's clearly a brilliant piece of work. Nick Twisp is a nearly pitch-perfect representation of the self-centered sociopathy and absurd arrogance of the intelligent teenager, taken to the nth degree. What American Psycho's Patrick Bateman was to disaffected yuppies, Nick Twisp is to arrogant, neurotic high school-aged boys.<br/><br/>The only problem is, I hate Nick so much that I can't face rereading the book very easily. <br/><br/>He's such a great anti-hero, and such a potentia</span>
  <span id="freeText14554963491629848515" style="display:none">I'm a bit conflicted about this book.<br /><br />It's clearly a brilliant piece of work. Nick Twisp is a nearly pitch-perfect representation of the self-centered sociopathy and absurd arrogance of the intelligent teenager, taken to the nth degree. What American Psycho's Patrick Bateman was to disaffected yuppies, Nick Twisp is to arrogant, neurotic high school-aged boys.<br /><br />The only problem is, I hate Nick so much that I can't face rereading the book very easily. <br /><br />He's such a great anti-hero, and such a potentially unreliable narrator, and such a... <i>shit</i>. Repeatedly through the middle and end of the book, I found myself cringing or squirming uncomfortably at the way he described or justified (or more often, didn't bother justifying) his actions.<br /><br />I have to acknowledge that at least some of this is that I feel so distinctly that Nick is a (grossly distorted and exaggerated) mirror of my internal life at around his age. The sense of dissociation, the obsessive love, and the ability to be deeply self-analyzing without developing any real awareness all hit a bit too close to home for me.<br /><br />Nonetheless, as a piece of writing, the book is great. My four-star rating reflects only my own hangups, not specific flaws in the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14554963491629848515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192447577?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/5550243-rebecca">Rebecca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192447577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1822265091014260865">God, this book was like soo painful to get through. It took me like 3 weeks to finally finish it. If you didn't know, this book is HUGE. It's like 500 pages. I took it with me to SF, as my old book, thinking maybe I'll make a dent in it if it's the only thing I bring (plus the awesome Jodi book). But no, I kept putting it off and finished the Jodi book in like 3 days. Anyway, I forced myself to finish it and while I feel successful in finishing something that was painful, it just brought nothing</span>
  <span id="freeText1822265091014260865" style="display:none">God, this book was like soo painful to get through. It took me like 3 weeks to finally finish it. If you didn't know, this book is HUGE. It's like 500 pages. I took it with me to SF, as my old book, thinking maybe I'll make a dent in it if it's the only thing I bring (plus the awesome Jodi book). But no, I kept putting it off and finished the Jodi book in like 3 days. Anyway, I forced myself to finish it and while I feel successful in finishing something that was painful, it just brought nothing new to my life. It's sort of written in journal format, but like with excruciating detail. It's supposed to be in the voice of a dude, but no dude would ever go into this much detail about anything in life. The protag was an asshole who just ran amok and didn't care about anything or anyone, including himself. Takes place in various places around NorCal and since the book was written in like 1994, I liked the dated-ness of it all. But the details were painful. And when the kids "alter ego" came into play, I had no idea what was going on for like 100 pages. But in the span of 500 pages, 100 is nothing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1822265091014260865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1177534-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781433251931" href="/book/show/3594967-youth-in-revolt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1177534-michael?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90516347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9628513199892236474">Curious about the movie of the same name, I figured I'd give the audio book of "Youth in Revolt" a chance.<br/><br/>Maybe it's the audio book format, but the story of Nick Twisp wasn't one that had me hurrying back or eager to continue to follow his exploits in the next books in the series. Nick is your average 14 year old teenager who is obsessed with sex and will do anything to try and rid himself to gain a girlfriend. During a summer vacation, he meets Sheeni Saunders, who he spends a week with and fal</span>
  <span id="freeText9628513199892236474" style="display:none">Curious about the movie of the same name, I figured I'd give the audio book of "Youth in Revolt" a chance.<br /><br />Maybe it's the audio book format, but the story of Nick Twisp wasn't one that had me hurrying back or eager to continue to follow his exploits in the next books in the series. Nick is your average 14 year old teenager who is obsessed with sex and will do anything to try and rid himself to gain a girlfriend. During a summer vacation, he meets Sheeni Saunders, who he spends a week with and falls head over heels in love with. But there are two huge problems. One is she lives 400 miles away and the other is she has a boyfriend.<br /><br />The story is told via journal entries by Nick and, at first, his observations are humorous. However, as the story goes along both he and Sheeni become more and more unlikeable, leading to my not really caring what happened to them by the end of the novel. Nick's idea of inventing multiple personas for himself potential but isn't really fully realized. Maybe it gets better in future books but for now I won't be eager to try them to find out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9628513199892236474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6177974429304684370">Oh to be 15 and awkward again. Wait, no, actually, I'd prefer the opposite. Being a teenager is awkward, confusing, strange. Parents don't seem to understand how your needs change as you get older. They don't seem to have any idea what kind of life you really lead. If you weren't born privileged, gorgeous, or a combination of both, chances are, the pretty guy or girl at the lake isn't going to fall madly for you unless you have a few tricks up your sleeve.<br/><br/>This is a book for the nice guys who are</span>
  <span id="freeText6177974429304684370" style="display:none">Oh to be 15 and awkward again. Wait, no, actually, I'd prefer the opposite. Being a teenager is awkward, confusing, strange. Parents don't seem to understand how your needs change as you get older. They don't seem to have any idea what kind of life you really lead. If you weren't born privileged, gorgeous, or a combination of both, chances are, the pretty guy or girl at the lake isn't going to fall madly for you unless you have a few tricks up your sleeve.<br /><br />This is a book for the nice guys who are tired of finishing last, the average kids who often have to contend with their exceptional peers, and if nothing else, a reminder to the hormone rage that no matter how much you want her, most girls aren't worth going to jail for. This book is painfully honest, funny, and even dark at times. As crazy as Nick gets, it still feels real. <br /><br />Don't see the movie; it's a disappointment even with the hilarity of Michael Cera's portrayal of Nick Twisp's alter ego. </span>

<div id="review_307893843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307893843" />
    <a title="Andrea Talarico" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7566862-andrea-talarico"><img alt="Andrea Talarico" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327888579p2/7566862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307893843?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Talarico" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Talarico" href="/user/show/7566862-andrea-talarico">Andrea Talarico</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307893843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10469042255788228653">14-year-old Nick Twisp is a swirling cesspool of hormones, humor, and angst. His divorced parents land somewhere on the Running with Scissors scale: self-obsessed, womanizing father; overbearing-yet-somehow oblivious mother, but neither are abusive like in Burroughs’ memoir. Nick’s best friend Lefty provides a much-needed outlet for Nick’s ramblings, but Lefty lacks Nick’s precocious intelligence, as well as his love of literature. Nick spends most of the book pining after a cute, smart girl. Yo</span>
  <span id="freeText10469042255788228653" style="display:none">14-year-old Nick Twisp is a swirling cesspool of hormones, humor, and angst. His divorced parents land somewhere on the Running with Scissors scale: self-obsessed, womanizing father; overbearing-yet-somehow oblivious mother, but neither are abusive like in Burroughs’ memoir. Nick’s best friend Lefty provides a much-needed outlet for Nick’s ramblings, but Lefty lacks Nick’s precocious intelligence, as well as his love of literature. Nick spends most of the book pining after a cute, smart girl. You see, Nick is just dying to lose his virginity – heck, even to kiss a girl. The author must have kept a diary as religiously as his protagonist does, because he navigates through the mind of a teenage boy like no other writer I’ve ever read. This book is hilariously funny and intelligently written. Nick reads like a mixture of Salinger’s Holden Caufield, Philip Roth’s Alex Portnoy, and the actor Michael Cera, who played Nick the movie based on this novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10469042255788228653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666526799" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer666526799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8445328750091007468">A little of <i>Youth in Revolt</i>'s narrator, 14-year-old Nick Twisp, goes a long way, so it's a calculated risk for author Payne to set his main character's hyper-articulate, sex-obsessed voice loose over 500 mammoth pages. It pays off, though, as <i>Youth in Revolt</i> ultimately proves itself to be adolescent turmoil told on an epic (and epically funny) scale. While the overarching story deals with Nick's pursuit of the beautiful and elusive (and sadistic, in the way only beautiful and elusive women can b</span>
  <span id="freeText8445328750091007468" style="display:none">A little of <i>Youth in Revolt</i>'s narrator, 14-year-old Nick Twisp, goes a long way, so it's a calculated risk for author Payne to set his main character's hyper-articulate, sex-obsessed voice loose over 500 mammoth pages. It pays off, though, as <i>Youth in Revolt</i> ultimately proves itself to be adolescent turmoil told on an epic (and epically funny) scale. While the overarching story deals with Nick's pursuit of the beautiful and elusive (and sadistic, in the way only beautiful and elusive women can be) Sheeni Saunders, Payne sets it against the backdrop of RV parks, labor strikes, cross-dressing, brushes with the law, neglectful parents, reincarnated dogs, and, oh yeah, lots and lots of sexual obsession. It's a labyrinthine plot of double- and triple-crosses, romantic assignations too numerous to count, duplicitous friends, and questionable motives, but Nick's voice – sarcastic, profane, and erudite – is the north star guiding the reader confidently through the madness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8445328750091007468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5751379439303599298" style="display:none">Nichole Marcy<br />YA - Humor<br /><br />C.D. Payne’s Youth in Revolt will have readers snorting and giggling like an insane 14 year old throughout the entire book. Nick Twisp is the hero of his own diary and Sheeni is his leading lady. He pines for her the moment he meets her, and as his diary progresses, he manages to to get kicked out of his school, burn down Berkley, and dress like an elderly woman, Carlotta. All in the name of love. He spends most of the time bouncing back and forth between his father’s house, where he lusts after his father’s 20 year old girlfriend and he is treated like a servant, and his mother’s house (the “Corndog Queen”) and her trucker boyfriend, Jerry. Does Nick Twisp get the girl, or does his alter-ego, Francois end up in jail? </span>

Soon one thing leads to another, which leads to youth in exile (part 3), which leads to total chaos.<br /><br />It's a 500 page book you'll read in 3 days, honest!</span>
